## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how the reaction rate depends on the concentration of reactants, possibly with various orders and mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration, constant rate'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to square of concentration (bimolecular reaction of same species)'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate dependence on concentration'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'Forward and reverse first-order reactions approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order / competing reactions', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Parallel first and second order reaction pathways'}
- {'name': 'Saturation kinetics (enzyme-like)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1)', 'scenario': 'Substrate-limited reaction rate with saturation'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where product catalyzes reaction'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent rate (photochemical)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate with time-dependent external driving (e.g., light intensity change)'}
- {'name': 'Fractional order with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'Fractional order kinetics with a constant source/sink term'}
- {'name': 'Second-order with equilibrium', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2', 'scenario': 'Quadratic rate law with equilibrium and constant production terms'}
- {'name': 'Cooperative kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2)', 'scenario': 'Cooperative or sigmoidal rate dependence on concentration'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate (consumption) with power-law dependence on concentration → dA_dt = -k * A^n, classic rate law
- Constant term in rate expression → indicates zero-order contribution or constant production/inflow of species
- Quadratic concentration dependence → suggests bimolecular reaction mechanism or dimerization
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic-type mechanism where both reactant and product matter
- Rate that changes sign at specific concentration → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium concentration
- Rational function of A → enzyme-mediated or surface-catalyzed reaction with saturation effects
- Weak or no explicit time dependence → autonomous kinetics where rate depends only on current state (concentration)
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system with external forcing, catalyst deactivation, or varying conditions

## Summary

The candidates that match are those that can express exactly `c_a*A^(1/3) + c_b*A + c_c*A*exp(c_d*t)`:

- **Candidate 8**: ✓ (set c0=0, c7=0, c2=1/3, c4=1)
- **Candidate 10**: ✓ (set c6=0, c1=0, c3=1)
- **Candidate 13**: ✓ (set c1=1/3, c3=1, c6=0)
